< Review>
I write for a music and coffee blog called Crooners In Coffeeshops, in which I interview local musicians at local coffeeshops. My writeup reflects the positive experience that I encountered at Go Get Em Tiger on our interview date.

Go Get ‚ÄòEm Tiger has come to be known as a beloved L.A coffee chain with roots in many foot traffic heavy neighborhoods. Opened in 2018, the Highland Park location found a home in a cute little small business cul-de-sac style building on the illustrious Figueroa Street, accompanied by Triple Beam Pizza and Highland Park Wine. Sound the alarm! You can get coffee, pizza AND wine in the the same hub!

Anyways, due to sharing a space with other businesses, GGET HP‚Äôs shop size is a bit smaller than some of their other locations, but that‚Äôs not to say that they don‚Äôt utilize their space to its fullest potential. A clean color palette of white and their signature light blue paired with luscious green plants hanging from the ceiling and light, warm wood display shelves (which also include plants and coffee making items). Plus, they have a cute indoor patio area for happy customers to enjoy their delicious coffee and healthy noms (if they don‚Äôt want pizza of course). All in all, the GGET team has done it again with a lovely location for locals to enjoy.< /Review>

< review>
Really dig this place for working. They've got free, passwordless wifi, great coffee, and ample seating. I'll note that the seating isn't entirely indoors which, because it's LA, is totally fine almost all of the time. There were a couple days this summer that I found myself pretty warm and I can imagine it gets chilly in the winter, but I'm not one to complain about our almost perfect weather in Southern California. The space is shared with Triple Beam (my favorite pizza in LA) and Hippo--also just a very hip part of HLP.

I usually just stick with the coffee and cold brew here, both of which I like. I've gotten the Business & Pleasure one as well which has three little fun coffee and tea drinks, but honestly is maybe overkill for my needs. They've got some breakfast-y foods that I haven't tried (because pizza), but it's nice to know they're available. Parking is easy and free on the side streets off Figueroa. Lovely addition to the neighborhood!< /review>

0 STARS!

Where do I begin...

Honestly, the first place to begin is reading the previous reviews, I read them last March when I was doing research on where to move, and I disregarded them thinking that maybe the issues were a one time thing. Now reading all other reviews I realize I am not alone and that there are large issues within the complex.

First and foremost, bugs, there is a serious issue with not only cockroaches at The Village, but there are silverfish as well. We were treated twice, please note you will have to leave, and the exterminators don't even know what they are treating the apartment for, it's extremely unorganized, if we weren't there they would've sprayed for ants. Outside at night you will find large cockroaches which are larger than mice, and sometimes you will find them squashed on the sidewalk.

If you have more than one car, be prepared for absolutely no parking, everytime you come home the majority of the time there is a tow truck that comes around. This didn't affect me, but the reviews are true, you will most likely get fined or towed.

Neighbors...be prepared to almost get run over as nobody follows the rules of the road, and I have witnessed others who are walking their dogs who almost get hit, I had this happen to myself on numerous occasions. Not only do people speed through the streets, but from my experience the neighbors below would refuse to take their garbage to the common trash area. They would throw their garbage into the trash bins next to the mailboxes. This was an ongoing issue, which after going to resident services and reporting it over 2 months, I stopped going, as the neighbors were only given warnings.
*If you have a dog, I would strongly advise not moving here for the safety of your animal when you are out taking them on a walk on the sidewalk area.

The best part...moving out:
We did a pre-move out inspection before we moved out. We were told that the carpets were installed in 2014, and that they were going to replace the carpets after we moved out regardless and we would not be charged. We had a form completed as well, which was for this purpose, which specified the areas that we would get charged, this line item was shown as N/A as these were going to be replaced. Fast forward, to now we were told that it was an estimate and we were charged for one year prorated which comes to $361 to replace the carpet. I spoke with the customer service center and was told there was nothing that could be done, and sorry for the miscommunication. I truly feel this is unacceptable, I want to share my experience as this clearly happens to countless others.

In conclusion, I wouldn't give them any stars as nothing can be resolved by their customer service. You will be advised to call their office number, which again it's a friendly well sorry for the miscommunication better luck next time.

Cheers, to not living in an overpriced, bug infested complex any longer.

I wish you all the best in your search!</text>

Prior to the Irvine Company taking over, I would have rated this place a 5 on their main pool and a 3 on the overall community due to crime, but now I'm rating this a 1.
- Crime has gotten much worse, where there are now squatters living in empty apartments. We pay for security guards to watch the neighborhood, but cops laugh at the amount of crime we have, saying they would never park their cars in our complex.
- The new management has managed to screw everything up. I had to sign-up for paying my water directly to NWP using Irvine's instructions, but then the Irvine company cancelled my account # but continued to bill me through NWP using my old account #, so I couldn't pay it online or over the phone.  The bill was also $180/month for water. Normally this was $40-$50, but after construction crews tapped into our building's water, our "share" increased by 4x. No credit seen as of yet.
- The management team posts notifications on our doors right before major holidays. One posting was to say we need to keep our lights on and trash put away if we are traveling, but their postings basically marked the homes where people were not home. Another posting was that we needed to vacate in January (posted 1 week before Christmas) for building upgrades, or stay through our lease-end and deal with the construction. They said we needed to let them know our January move decision by February 1st...they're idiots.
- We've asked for increased security, but they refuse to fix street lights, security cameras, improve fencing, or even install a gate at the entrance. It's so bad that kids hopped the fence to play basketball on the courts at 2am, and the security couldn't do anything about it as their keys wouldn't let them into the courts (and calling the cops wasn't a part of their escalation matrix).
- The plants are also covered in dog mess.  I blame the pet owners for this, but the management team should be enforcing their pet rules more.

We will be moving to a new place, and I highly recommend anyone searching for cheap places to rent to consider the various comments written about this place pointing out crime, poor management, and pet mess.<//review>

< review>
I had a 7:45am appointment. The Tech seemed like she was in a rush. I didn't catch her name but she had dark hair and was in the very last station. When it was time to take my blood, she prepped my arm. I usually turn away during the stick, so I wasn't looking, but after the initial pinch there was a sharp tingling pain that traveled the length of my arm. I immediately turned to look what happened and no blood was coming out. The tech had to pull it back and fish a little to find my vein. My gut is that she when thru my vein. I unfortunately had to leave right away because I was gonna be late for work, but I was able to call the office. I spoke with the supervisor named Kelsey. She apologized, and said that she would forward the information to the manager and they would follow up with me to see how I was doing. She said to call if I had any questions and explained some of the symptoms that I might get for a day or so. She mentioned that there is always a high risk that this will happen, but also stated that the tech should have known better. I did call on Monday to speak about my arm still tingling, and the person that answered the phone said that she would have the Manager call me about it. I received no call. I ended up going to my doctor and asking my questions there. My doctor was more than a little surprised that this happened. In their opinion, I apparently am an easy stick. She asked if the tech was a student, and I stated no. My doctor stated that this is a common mistake for students, but an experienced tech would not have done this. My doctor then informed me that my symptoms would be there for possibly a week. It is now FRIDAY. NO ONE has called me. NO ONE has followed up. I don't even know if my issue was even escalated to the Manager because when I originally asked for them on Monday the person that answered was hesitant to even let me talk to them. I told them what happened and she seemed very uninterested and unconcerned. I obviously don't need medical assistance any longer, since I have already gone to my doctor with my concerns. But, from the stand point of customer service, you should consider actually following thru with your patients. ESPECIALLY, when your technician was at fault.< /review>

<UserId.>103326374072263472284<//UserId.>< Name>
Tony Gravagno<//Name>
< date>
1475086346604</date>
<rate>5< /rate>< review>
Everything has been great for me.

I've been to this office before and didn't have the bad experience conveyed by others. So I wanted to give them another chance.

Before I start, I'm not denying anyone else's experience and the bad reviews here. I'm just conveying my experience which happens to be different. Take that as you will.

But as to "no more walk-ins", that's completely incorrect. The phone line for Quest says "walk-ins are always welcome". I called for an appointment but it said the earliest available slot was in two days. I already fasted for a blood test so I just went in. There is a sign-in sheet for appointments and walk-ins. Hardly anyone was there (Wednesday AM). I got in with no problem.

I was told that on Saturdays they get a lot of people with appointments and the walk-ins fill up the rest of the schedule early in the morning. That's basic "first-come first-serve", and "overflow" can't be served. That's just a matter of basic resources - limits on personnel and time. So yes, it's possible that some people will get turned away if they see the schedule is completely filled.

As to wait time, it really depends on when you get there and pure luck. You can't call to find out how busy they are. A lot of people with appointments don't show up, but if they do then walk-ins need to wait behind them.

They do more than blood there, it's all body fluids, so wait time is not just dependent on whether you're getting a blood test or something else. If you really just need blood work, consider another an office that doesn't provide all of the other services too.

My personal experience today, Wednesday 9/28: I got in at 9:30AM, was called in at 9:40ish after they processed about 3 other people. The phlebotomist was done with me by 9:47. I had to give them urine and was out of the office by 9:55. I've had to wait longer in the past but I was still in and out within an hour. Working for myself I can get in while other people work 9-5 jobs. That's a huge factor which makes it more difficult for 9-5 workers and students but good for others like seniors.

As to quality and service. My contact was cordial and professional, efficient during the blood draw, conversational but not overly chatty. This was the best possible experience.

As a side note, there is a small street that goes around the parking lot and there is usually a space available, so it's free parking there if you can walk up a couple steps to get to the building. I don't know if they charge for parking in the lot but in my few visits I've never had to find out.

Everywhere we go we will find occasional delays and bad service, and we should report it in review places like this. But we should also balance the good experience reviews with the bad to see if a place has frequent problems or if there was just a bad day or two. Given my experiences which have been completely different from some others here, I'd say this place is fine with occasional common issues. For me a lot more bad reports would be needed for me to second-guess that impression.

I hope that helps others...< /review>

1617883845591</Date>
< Rate>
5< /Rate>
<Text>I've been to a lot of antique stores before, but never like this one. I didn't fully experience and walk around the store fully because I was filled with a lot of emotion. It's not a bad thing, but rather good. I was slapped with memories that I haven't thought of in....... well since I last experienced them. This store felt like I was walking into past, like I was actually walking inside my memories. It was a good cry back to memory lane.

There is parking in front of the store and on the side, but go for the side parking. It'll be much easier to get back onto the road. The moment I walked in I was pessimistic due to the fact they had an old wheel chair in foyer. I walked in and I was literally surprised. It wasn't cluttered and I didn't feel bombarded with a mountain of junk. This place was clean too. The floor was open and the antiques and not much older items was spread out nicely. They had some really nice vintage items and items my grandparents had as wells as my mom's. That is why I was flushed with emotional tears.  LOL I started thinking to myself....."So, this is the place where our things went when we can't find it, or lose them, or throw them away. Maybe my personal gremlin owns that store and he was selling me my things back." The guy inside was really cool. He didn't follow me or kept an eye on me and just let me browse around. Not like other antique stores were they follow you around with their peripheral or pretend to put things away. It's unfortunate I didn't walk around the store fully because there were a lot of things that reminded me of my grandparents and my mom. I would totally recommend this place.<//Text>< pictures>
None<//pictures>

< Review>
I came across this place in another search engine about a year ago and went to try it out but, unfortunately, the outside facade left much to be desired and I ended up passing on it. Then it came up again just recently and with lots of good reviews so I decided to give it a try, again. It‚Äôs just a small local diner with really friendly wait staff and great cooks. I ordered the Country Fried Steak plate and it was one of the best I‚Äôve had: the steak was good and gravy delicious; the house potatoes were moist and came with onions and peppers (if you desire); and the soft scrambled eggs I ordered were just as I asked- fluffy and yellow with no burnt parts.  I didn‚Äôt give 5 stars because the curbside appeal leaves much to be desired. A few little colorfully painted signs on the windows might go far to make this place more inviting and bring in more clients. Don‚Äôt let your first impression fool you. Go in.</Review>

Nice little place for dinner. Initially thought they were closed, it seemed dark and there weren't any lighted signs that I noticed. But we've driven by a few times and I've been wanting to try it out, so we pulled into the parking lot saw the open sign and an elderly couple heading in the door and stopped in ourselves.
